[10/17/2021 11:36 AM] apexpool#3878
I saw that changing REF_PER in the last test brought a good improvement, but I cannot find it on the Vega56 cards


[10/17/2021 11:37 AM] Wolf9466#6211
REF_PER on the FPGA is REF on the Vega cards - it is just the refresh rate, but it's expressed in REF_PER - which is time_interval / tCK.


[10/17/2021 11:37 AM] apexpool#3878
this is what a Asus Rog Strix Vega56 with Hynix memory has as default ```# amdmemtweak --current
GPU 0:  Vega 10 XL/XT [Radeon RX Vega 56/64]    pci:0000:05:00.0
Memory state: 800MHz
Memory: Hynix HBM2
Memory vendor and model 63AB1A9C
Timing 1:      CL: 18      RAS: 24      RCDRD: 22      RCDWR: 10
Timing 2:      RCAb (RC): 37      RCPb (RC): 37      RPAb (RP): 13      RPPb (RP): 13
Timing 3:      RRDS: 3      RRDL: 3      RTP: 6
Timing 4:      FAW: 13
Timing 5:      CWL: 6      WTRS: 4      WTRL: 4
Timing 6:      WR: 12
Timing 7:      RREFD: 7
Timing 8:      RDRDDD: 3      RDRDSD: 2      RDRDSC: 1      RDRDSCL: 3
Timing 9:      WRWRDD: 3      WRWRSD: 2      WRWRSC: 1      WRWRSCL: 3
Timing 10:      WRRD: 1      RDWR: 18
Timing 12:      REF: 3200
Timing 13:      MRD: 4      MOD: 12
Timing 14:      XS: 216
Timing 16:      XSMRS: 216
Timing 17:      PD: 7        CKSRE: 8      CKSRX: 8
Timing 20:      RFCPB: 96      STAG: 7
Timing 21:      XP: 7        CPDED: 2      CKE: 7
Timing 22:      RDDATA: 17      WRLAT: 4      RDLAT: 14      WRDATA: 1
Timing 23:      CKESTAG: 2
RFC Timing:      RFC: 176```


[10/17/2021 11:38 AM] Wolf9466#6211
also, you're running at 800Mhz, I'm running at 1200, our timings will differ due to this.


[10/17/2021 11:38 AM] Wolf9466#6211
Remember that timings, unless explicitly specified otherwise, are actually not units in nanoseconds or similar, but ticks of tCK - the memory clock.

{Reactions}
üëç 

[10/17/2021 11:38 AM] apexpool#3878
847MHz seems to be the best value


[10/17/2021 11:39 AM] Wolf9466#6211
This effectively means that every time you change the memclock, the timings change ever so slightly (or not so slightly, depending on the memclk change)


[10/17/2021 11:39 AM] apexpool#3878
I believe decreasing RCDRD brings the most MH/s


[10/17/2021 11:41 AM] Wolf9466#6211
Besides REF, you mean? Yeah, it's one of the biggest. It's ACTIVATE command to READ command delay.


[10/17/2021 11:41 AM] apexpool#3878
not besides REF, from all.


[10/17/2021 11:41 AM] Wolf9466#6211
If you leave REF at stock, you'll be surprised how much of an effect it has :3


[10/17/2021 11:41 AM] Wolf9466#6211
Since Ergo is doing 32-byte small accesses, at random addresses, though - tRCDRD is a strong contender for most important timing


[10/17/2021 11:42 AM] Wolf9466#6211
because effectively, random addresses means you've basically no chance of hitting the same row twice, one directly after the other - it's just VERY improbable


[10/17/2021 11:43 AM] Wolf9466#6211
Because of the fact you may only have one row per bank activated, you need to close (PRECHARGE) that row before you do the next access within that bank.


[10/17/2021 11:44 AM] Wolf9466#6211
So, an ACTIVATE command is issued for a row, then tRCDRD clocks must happen BEFORE you are allowed to issue a READ from that row.


[10/17/2021 11:44 AM] Wolf9466#6211
This will happen REAL often, because as I said - random addressing.


[10/17/2021 11:44 AM] apexpool#3878
so it's faster memory access when tRCDRD is less


[10/17/2021 11:44 AM] Wolf9466#6211
Correct.


[10/17/2021 11:45 AM] Wolf9466#6211
This applies to Ergo more than it would for, say, Ethash. Don't get me wrong, it matters for Ethash, but not *quite* as much because it loads 128 bytes at a time.


[10/17/2021 11:46 AM] Wolf9466#6211
This means it gets to use the ability of the memory to "burst" read: it reads several 32 byte chunks from the same row, one after another. It does not have to PRECHARGE the row and ACTIVATE another - it just gets all 128 bytes.


[10/17/2021 11:47 AM] Wolf9466#6211
btw...


[10/17/2021 11:48 AM] Wolf9466#6211
having tFAW > tRRD * 4 makes little sense :3


[10/17/2021 11:48 AM] Wolf9466#6211
It's not harmful, just strange.


[10/17/2021 11:48 AM] apexpool#3878
it's the default


[10/17/2021 11:49 AM] Wolf9466#6211
*shrugs* It's not sensible, but it's okay.


[10/17/2021 11:49 AM] apexpool#3878
which RRD?


[10/17/2021 11:49 AM] apexpool#3878
```Timing 3:      RRDS: 3      RRDL: 3      RTP: 6```


[10/17/2021 11:50 AM] apexpool#3878
these 2?


[10/17/2021 11:50 AM] apexpool#3878
should tFAW be decreased, or RRD increased? @Wolf9466


[10/17/2021 11:51 AM] Wolf9466#6211
tFAW decreased by 1.


[10/17/2021 11:52 AM] Wolf9466#6211
The reason is, tFAW is Four Activate Window - it's a rolling window of clock cycles during which ONLY four ACTIVATE commands may be issued (remember, they all have to be to different banks!)


[10/17/2021 11:53 AM] Wolf9466#6211
Because tRRD is the amount of clocks you must wait between ACTIVATE'ing in one bank, and ACTIVATE'ing in another, 4 * tRRD is literally the most tFAW can be: this is because only four activates can take place during 4 * tRRD clocks.


[10/17/2021 11:54 AM] apexpool#3878
```Timing 3:      RRDS: 3      RRDL: 6      RTP: 5
Timing 4:      FAW: 12
```


[10/17/2021 11:54 AM] apexpool#3878
this is for the Samsung Vega56 card, as it's running now


[10/17/2021 11:54 AM] apexpool#3878
and default was ```Timing 3:      RRDS: 4      RRDL: 5      RTP: 5
Timing 4:      FAW: 13
```


[10/17/2021 11:54 AM] Wolf9466#6211
Ah, it was 13 because RRDL was 5


[10/17/2021 11:55 AM] Wolf9466#6211
and 4 * 4 is 16, 13 < 16, so makes sense (RRDS)


[10/17/2021 11:55 AM] Wolf9466#6211
you can leave FAW alone as your settings are - but the "default", IMO, should probably be corrected


[10/17/2021 11:55 AM] Wolf9466#6211
just cause it's a bad example


[10/17/2021 11:58 AM] apexpool#3878

[10/29/2021 9:04 AM] Attila#3944
Minor change in my rig üòÑ flipped all my Hynix cards and sourced 12 Gigabyte brand cards with Samsung RAM. Last one is still shipping. Spent weeks managing this. Conclusions: batch of 3 OC Eagles from Cyberport seem to be very power-hungry. There is one Gaming OC Pro from the 3.0 LHR generation, that one has an 8+6 pin power supply, that one is also hungry. Some Eagles can do 150-152MH/s at 110W. Will have to figure out what works for each one. Also, I could sell all my Hynix cards used at a higher price point when compared to what I bought them at a month ago. All in all, the upgrade barely cost a couple hundred Euros. Hashrate increase is 15-20% at this point.

[11/01/2021 6:06 PM] geezar#8187
` --lhr-tune                 [Ethash, Autolykos2] LHR tuning value that indicates the percentage of the full speed the miner
                                   tries to achieve for LHR cards (default: -1). Range from 10 to 95.
                                   -1 - auto-mode (LHR tune is set to 71 (or 68 in low power mode) for LHR cards and 0 for non-LHR)
                                    0 - disabled (use for non-LHR cards)
                                   30 - recommended starting value for most LHR cards in LHR unlock dual mining mode (see --lhr-algo)
                                   68 - recommended starting value for most LHR cards in low power mode (see --lhr-low-power)
                                   71 - recommended starting value for most LHR cards
                                   Can be set for each GPU separately, e.g.`

[11/11/2021 10:37 AM] geezar#8187
I know, same here üôÇ Overdrivetool is just a different way to control the fan/clocks - you can do the same natively in the tweaker but depending on the AMD drivers I used sometimes the fans would not play ball - imagine now its probably just an overhead. I used to run a bat file to apply the tweaks + the overdrivent clocks at boot time with a delay allowing the miner to start then adding the tweaks. Windows was a hassle but with some effort can be automated/stable

[08/19/2022 2:56 AM] soupy#0476
new drivers wont work with t-rex however  nb miner works fine I noticed this on nicehash I found this - NVIDIA released a new driver version on May 24th. NVIDIA 512.95 driver do not work with the 100% LHR unlock.

We tested the unlock with the latest drivers on all verified miners, also included in NiceHash Miner. NiceHash QuickMiner (Excavator), NBMiner NanoMiner, and LolMiner.

If you are already on the NVIDIA driver version 512.95, then for now, we suggest downgrading to NVIDIA driver version 512.77 where the unlock still works.

[09/09/2022 3:22 PM] Ciufcia#1746
Hello, I made this doc with OC, AMD cards are a little bit weird but overall this should work nicely. Every model of card was tested on full rig of 12 GPUS or like in case of 3090 and 3080TI on full rig of 8 GPUS. This should be stable in most cases, but the power really depends from manufacturer. 3060TI (H) means 3060TI with Hynix memory. NVIDIA miner was trex and AMD was teamredminer
5600XT has modified bios from bitby.ru and power draw should be lower than the one in my doc

Just so people know setting the --lock-cv 730 makes a difference on power if you don't do the --lock-cv 730 your power will be higher. for windows in HiveOS you can set it when you add miner and select miner config extra params put "lock-cv": "730" if you have 3000 series cards or you can "730,730,730,730" like that for mutliple cards 730 i recommend for 3000 series cards as i never tested on any other cards

[01/12/2023 1:01 AM] Sweetdjf#7448
Use afterburner and go into the curve editor. Click on a point starting at 800mv and press control+L to lock the core voltage, keep going down until the voltage is low enough to trigger power state 3, you will know when the memory speed drops considerably. Leave everything else alone. This is for best efficiency


[01/12/2023 8:37 AM] superfuru#4231
ok thanks
